## Domain Knowledge
**Domain**: chemical kinetics
**Analysis**: The task models the rate of change of concentration dA/dt as a function of concentration A and time t, which is classic reaction kinetics. Common rate laws express dA/dt as a function of A raised to a power (reaction order), possibly with timeŌĆædependence for nonŌĆæisothermal or catalystŌĆædeactivation effects.

**Common formula structures** (built-in generic + LLM domain-specific):
- Arrhenius equation: k = c0 * exp(c1 / T) (chemical reaction rate dependence on temperature)
- Coulomb's / Newton's inverse-square law: F = c0 / r**2 (gravitational or electrostatic force)
- Stefan-Boltzmann law: P = c0 * T**4 (blackbody radiation power vs temperature)
- Beer-Lambert law: I = c0 * exp(c1 * x) (light intensity attenuation through a medium)
- Michaelis-Menten kinetics: v = c0 * S / (S + c1) (enzyme-catalyzed reaction saturation)
- Hill equation: y = c0 * x**c1 / (x**c1 + c2) (cooperative binding, sigmoidal dose-response)
- Kepler's third law: T**2 = c0 * a**3 (orbital period vs semi-major axis)
- Newton's law of cooling: T = c0 + c1 * exp(c2 * t) (exponential thermal relaxation)
- Clausius-Clapeyron relation: log(P) = c0 + c1 / T (vapor pressure vs temperature)
- Langmuir adsorption isotherm: theta = c0 * P / (1 + c1 * P) (surface adsorption equilibrium)
- Freundlich isotherm: q = c0 * C**c1 (empirical adsorption on heterogeneous surface)
- Stokes' drag: F = c0 * r * v (viscous drag force on a sphere in fluid)
- Logistic growth: N = c0 / (1 + c1 * exp(c2 * t)) (population dynamics with carrying capacity)
- Planck-Wien approximation: I = c0 * f**3 * exp(c1 * f / T) (thermal radiation spectrum)
- FirstŌĆæorder irreversible: dA_dt = -c0 * A
- SecondŌĆæorder irreversible: dA_dt = -c0 * A**2
- nŌĆæth order irreversible: dA_dt = -c0 * A**c1
- ZeroŌĆæorder with firstŌĆæorder decay: dA_dt = c0 - c1 * A
- Reversible firstŌĆæorder (massŌĆæconserved): dA_dt = -c0 * A + c1 * (c2 - A)
- Autocatalytic (logistic) growth: dA_dt = c0 * A * (c1 - A)
- TimeŌĆædecaying rate constant: dA_dt = -c0 * A * exp(-c1 * t)
- Hyperbolic time dependence: dA_dt = -c0 * A / (c1 + t)
- Mixed secondŌĆæ and firstŌĆæorder: dA_dt = -c0 * A**2 - c1 * A
- HalfŌĆæorder decay: dA_dt = -c0 * sqrt(A)
- Substrate inhibition (bellŌĆæshaped rate): dA_dt = -c0 * A / (1 + c1 * A**2)
- Exponential autocatalysis: dA_dt = c0 * A * exp(-c1 * A)
- GompertzŌĆætype decay: dA_dt = -c0 * A * log(c1 * A)
- Parallel zeroŌĆæ and firstŌĆæorder: dA_dt = -c0 - c1 * A
- FractionalŌĆæorder with timeŌĆædependent coefficient: dA_dt = -c0 * t**c1 * A**c2

**Formula structure heuristic features**:
- Oscillation damping envelope ŌåÆ Exponential decay envelope f(x)*exp(-c*Abs(x)) for symmetric damped oscillation, Gaussian envelope f(x)*exp(-c*x**2) for localized wave packets
- Saturation/clipping effects ŌåÆ Rational fraction x/(1+x), tanh; for variables with alternating positive/negative in oscillatory systems, selectively apply Abs
- Growth/decay ŌåÆ Exponential growth exp(c*t), Logistic 1/(1+exp(-c*x)), power law x**c
- Threshold/activation behavior ŌåÆ Max(x-c, 0), piecewise functions
- Coupling/cross effects ŌåÆ Product terms between variables x*y, power-law coupling x**c1 * y**c2
- Exact proportionality of rate to A (dA_dt ŌłØ A) implies firstŌĆæorder kinetics.
- PowerŌĆælaw dependence dA_dt ŌłØ A^n (n ŌēĀ 1) indicates nŌĆæth order reaction; integer n often corresponds to molecularity.
- Presence of a positive term like c0*A*(c1ŌĆæA) signals autocatalysis with a carrying capacity (sigmoid growth).
- Explicit time t appearing multiplicatively or in denominators suggests catalyst deactivation or external timeŌĆævarying conditions.
- Rate that first rises then falls with A can be captured by inhibition forms like dA_dt = -A/(1 + c*A^2).
- A constant term (independent of A) in the rate expression corresponds to zeroŌĆæorder behaviour, typical of saturated catalytic surfaces.
- Sum of multiple powers of A (e.g., c0*A + c1*A^2) points to parallel reactions of different orders.
- Logarithmic dependence on A in the rate law arises from complex cooperative or heterogeneous mechanisms (e.g., Gompertz kinetics).
- A term of the form exp(ŌĆæc1*t) multiplied by a function of A indicates an exponentially decaying effective rate constant.
- A denominator containing (c1 + t) models a rate constant that decays hyperbolically with time.

I need to compare each candidate against the Ground Truth (GT):

**GT:** `-0.3122*A*exp(-0.0798*t) + 0.4717*sin(0.8722*A)`

The GT has two terms:
1. `A*exp(c*t)` ŌĆö an exponential decay in t multiplied by A
2. `sin(c*A)` ŌĆö a sine function of A (no phase shift, or equivalently phase = 0)

Note: The sine term in GT is `sin(0.8722*A)` with no additive phase constant. A candidate with `sin(A*c3 + c4)` can match if we set `c4 = 0`.

GT = A*exp(c*t) + sin(c*A) = [A*(A+c2)*exp(c*t) + (A+c2)*sin(c*A)] / (A+c2)
= [A┬▓*exp(c*t) + A*c2*exp(c*t) + A*sin(c*A) + c2*sin(c*A)] / (A+c2)

Comparing: c0 matches exp coefficient of A┬▓, c4 = c2*c0_gt... wait, let me be more careful.

Numerator of GT over (A+c2): A┬▓*exp(c1*t) * 1 + A*c2*exp(c1*t) + A*sin(cA) + c2*sin(cA) + A*c3_extra

We need c3=0 (to eliminate the A*c3 term that has no t-dependence and isn't sin). Then:
= [A*exp(c1*t)*(A*c0+c4) + sin(A*c6+c7)*(A*c5+c8)] / (A+c2)

For GT: need A*c0+c4 = A (so c0=1, c4=0... wait, that gives A┬▓*exp/A+c2). Actually we need (A*c0+c4) = k*(A+c2) for some k, so c4 = k*c2 and c0=k. Similarly c8 = c5*c2/c5... Let me set c0=k, c4=k*c2: numerator becomes k*A*(A+c2)*exp(c1*t) + sin(A*c6+c7)*(A*c5+c8). Then dividing by (A+c2): k*A*exp(c1*t) + sin(A*c6+c7)*(A*c5+c8)/(A+c2). Matches GT! Ō£ō
